    // Check if we're on a product page
    if ($('.product').length > 0) {
        
        // Get the current product ID
        var productId = null;
        
        // Method 1: Try to get product ID from body class
        $('body').attr('class').split(' ').forEach(function(className) {
            if (className.indexOf('postid-') === 0) {
                productId = parseInt(className.replace('postid-', ''));
            }
        });
        
        // Method 2: Try to get product ID from the URL
        if (!productId) {
            var urlParams = new URLSearchParams(window.location.search);
            if (urlParams.has('post') || urlParams.has('product_id')) {
                productId = parseInt(urlParams.get('post') || urlParams.get('product_id'));
            }
        }
        
        // Method 3: Try to get from product class
        if (!productId) {
            var productClass = $('.product').attr('class');
            if (productClass) {
                var matches = productClass.match(/post-(d+)/);
                if (matches && matches.length > 1) {
                    productId = parseInt(matches[1]);
                }
            }
        }
        
        // Method 4: Look for hidden input with product_id
        if (!productId) {

                productId = parseInt(hiddenInput);

					<a href="https://momaa.org/cambridge-surrenders-116-benin-bronzes-to-nigeria-and-the-british-museum-has-nowhere-left-to-hide/" class="post-thumbnail"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="450" height="300" src="https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/benin-bronzes-450x300.webp" class="attachment-konte-post-thumbnail-shortcode size-konte-post-thumbnail-shortcode wp-post-image" alt="Cambridge Surrenders 116 Benin Bronzes to Nigeria — and the British Museum Has Nowhere Left to Hide" srcset="https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/benin-bronzes-450x300.webp 450w, https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/benin-bronzes-100x68.webp 100w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 450px) 100vw, 450px" /></a>
					<div class="konte-post-grid__summary">
						<h5 class="post-title"><a href="https://momaa.org/cambridge-surrenders-116-benin-bronzes-to-nigeria-and-the-british-museum-has-nowhere-left-to-hide/" rel="bookmark">Cambridge Surrenders 116 Benin Bronzes to Nigeria — and the British Museum Has Nowhere Left to Hide</a></h5>
						<div class="post-summary"><span class="span-reading-time rt-reading-time" style="display: block;"><span class="rt-label rt-prefix">Reading Time:</span> <span class="rt-time"> 7</span> <span class="rt-label rt-postfix">minutes</span></span>The University of Cambridge has formally transferred ownership of 116 Benin Bronzes to Nigeria's National Commission for Museums and Monuments, completing a decade-long repatriation dialogue and establishing a legal precedent that other UK institutions can follow. The objects — cast brass commemorative heads, ceremonial plaques, and intricately worked regalia — were seized during the British military's 1897 sacking of Benin City. Physical repatriation is expected before the end of 2026, with works destined for museums in Lagos and Benin City. The move intensifies scrutiny on the British Museum, which holds approximately 900 Benin objects and remains the largest institutional holdout against repatriation. Cambridge's success in obtaining UK Charity Commission approval for the transfer dismantles the legal defence that other charitable trusts have cited as an insurmountable barrier to returning colonial-era seizures.</div>
						<a class="button alt" href="https://momaa.org/cambridge-surrenders-116-benin-bronzes-to-nigeria-and-the-british-museum-has-nowhere-left-to-hide/">Continue reading</a>
					</div>
				</div><div class="post-87151 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-architecture category-art-education category-blog category-museum-chronicle">
					<a href="https://momaa.org/the-empty-vitrine-how-africa-is-building-the-infrastructure-to-end-the-oldest-excuse-for-keeping-its-heritage/" class="post-thumbnail"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="450" height="300" src="https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/the-luxor-museum-of-ancient-egyptian-art-450x300.jpg" class="attachment-konte-post-thumbnail-shortcode size-konte-post-thumbnail-shortcode wp-post-image" alt="Luxor Museum Luxor" srcset="https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/the-luxor-museum-of-ancient-egyptian-art-450x300.jpg 450w, https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/05/the-luxor-museum-of-ancient-egyptian-art-100x68.jpg 100w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 450px) 100vw, 450px" /></a>
					<div class="konte-post-grid__summary">
						<h5 class="post-title"><a href="https://momaa.org/the-empty-vitrine-how-africa-is-building-the-infrastructure-to-end-the-oldest-excuse-for-keeping-its-heritage/" rel="bookmark">The Empty Vitrine: How Africa Is Building the Infrastructure to End the Oldest Excuse for Keeping Its Heritage</a></h5>
						<div class="post-summary"><span class="span-reading-time rt-reading-time" style="display: block;"><span class="rt-label rt-prefix">Reading Time:</span> <span class="rt-time"> 11</span> <span class="rt-label rt-postfix">minutes</span></span>For two centuries, Western museums told African nations: you cannot protect your own heritage. In 2026, that argument meets a billion-dollar museum on the Giza Plateau, 119 Benin Bronzes returned to Nigeria, a Manhattan DA unit that has recovered $470 million in looted antiquities, and an African Union framework that has elevated restitution from bilateral grievance to continental policy. The vitrines are filling. The question is who will be remembered as the last to let go.</div>
						<a class="button alt" href="https://momaa.org/the-empty-vitrine-how-africa-is-building-the-infrastructure-to-end-the-oldest-excuse-for-keeping-its-heritage/">Continue reading</a>
					</div>
				</div><div class="post-87147 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-blog">
					<a href="https://momaa.org/the-alchemy-of-refusal-el-anatsui-and-the-art-of-making-empires-visible-through-their-waste/" class="post-thumbnail"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="450" height="300" src="https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/download-450x300.jpeg" class="attachment-konte-post-thumbnail-shortcode size-konte-post-thumbnail-shortcode wp-post-image" alt="The Future of African Art Education: Developing Talent and Shaping Careers" srcset="https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/download-450x300.jpeg 450w, https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/download-897x598.jpeg 897w, https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/download-300x200.jpeg 300w, https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/download-1024x682.jpeg 1024w, https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/download-768x512.jpeg 768w, https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/download-100x68.jpeg 100w, https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/download-660x440.jpeg 660w, https://momaa.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/download.jpeg 1486w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 450px) 100vw, 450px" /></a>
					<div class="konte-post-grid__summary">
						<h5 class="post-title"><a href="https://momaa.org/the-alchemy-of-refusal-el-anatsui-and-the-art-of-making-empires-visible-through-their-waste/" rel="bookmark">The Alchemy of Refusal: El Anatsui and the Art of Making Empires Visible Through Their Waste</a></h5>
						<div class="post-summary"><span class="span-reading-time rt-reading-time" style="display: block;"><span class="rt-label rt-prefix">Reading Time:</span> <span class="rt-time"> 12</span> <span class="rt-label rt-postfix">minutes</span></span>The hype says El Anatsui turns scrap metal into gold. The reality is more disruptive: he turns colonial waste into objects so compelling that the very institutions built on that trade history cannot look away. At 81, with commissions from Tate to the Vienna Opera and a radical return to wood, Anatsui is redefining what a late career — and African art itself — demands of the world.</div>
						<a class="button alt" href="https://momaa.org/the-alchemy-of-refusal-el-anatsui-and-the-art-of-making-empires-visible-through-their-waste/">Continue reading</a>

    <script type="rocketlazyloadscript">
        // Filter functionality
        document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
            const filterTabs = document.querySelectorAll('.filter-tab');
            const calculatorCards = document.querySelectorAll('.calculator-card');

            filterTabs.forEach(tab => {
                tab.addEventListener('click', function() {
                    const category = this.getAttribute('data-category');
                    
                    // Update active tab
                    filterTabs.forEach(t => t.classList.remove('active'));
                    this.classList.add('active');
                    
                    // Filter cards
                    calculatorCards.forEach(card => {
                        if (category === 'all' || card.getAttribute('data-category') === category) {
                            card.style.display = 'block';
                            card.style.animation = 'fadeInUp 0.5s ease-out';
                        } else {
                            card.style.display = 'none';
                        }
                    });
                });
            });

            // Card hover effects
            calculatorCards.forEach(card => {
                card.addEventListener('mouseenter', function() {
                    this.style.transform = 'translateY(-5px)';
                });
                
                card.addEventListener('mouseleave', function() {
                    this.style.transform = 'translateY(0)';
                });
            });
        });

        // Animation keyframes
        const style = document.createElement('style');
        style.textContent = `
            @keyframes fadeInUp {
                from {
                    opacity: 0;
                    transform: translateY(30px);
                }
                to {
                    opacity: 1;
                    transform: translateY(0);
                }
            }
        `;
        document.head.appendChild(style);
    </script>

			<h3><span style="color: #ffffff;">Subscribe to MoMAA newsletter</span></h3>

<div class="konte-empty-space " style="height: 30px"></div></div></div></div></div><div class="vc_row-full-width vc_clearfix"></div><div class="vc_row wpb_row vc_row-fluid"><div class="wpb_column vc_column_container vc_col-sm-12"><div class="vc_column-inner"><div class="wpb_wrapper"><div class="konte-empty-space " aria-hidden="true"><div class="konte-empty-space__xs visible-xs" style="height:30px"></div><div class="konte-empty-space__sm visible-sm" style="height:60px"></div><div class="konte-empty-space__md visible-md" style="height:60px"></div><div class="konte-empty-space__lg visible-lg" style="height:60px"></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="vc_row wpb_row vc_row-fluid"><div class="wpb_column vc_column_container vc_col-sm-3"><div class="vc_column-inner"><div class="wpb_wrapper">
	<div class="wpb_text_column wpb_content_element" >
		<div class="wpb_wrapper">
			<h3>MoMAA &#8211; African Modern Art Gallery &amp; Lifestyle</h3>
<p>Stepping into the world of the <strong><a href="https://momaa.org/african-artist-spotlight-series-emeka-ogbohs-sonic-landscapes/" data-wpil-monitor-id="2843">African Modern Artist</a></strong>, one experiences an artful blend of eloquence, cultural savoir-faire, and an enviable cache of worldly experiences. Like a maestro wielding a baton, the artist conducts a symphony of narratives on the canvas of <a href="https://momaa.org/product-category/artworks/" target="_new" rel="noopener">Contemporary African Art</a>, touching upon the poignant themes of our time &#8211; from the planet&#8217;s pressing environmental concerns to the rise of women&#8217;s empowerment and the emotive tales of global diaspora.</p>
<h3>The Artistry</h3>
<p>Imagine, if you will, the <a href="https://momaa.org/zoma-museum-vs-museum-of-modern-art-of-algiers/" data-wpil-monitor-id="3492">artist at work &#8211; their hands deftly moving across</a> various artistic mediums, each stroke, click or adjustment bringing to life their unique vision of Africa. The result? A delightful assortment of immersive installations, evocative paintings, thought-provoking <a href="https://momaa.org/best-oversized-wall-art-ideas-large-canvas-abstract-art-for-big-walls/" data-wpil-monitor-id="930">sculptures</a>, striking photography, and compelling film that tell the African story in ways words often fail to capture.</p>
<h3>The Market Trends</h3>
<p>The art market, much like the whimsical world of <a href="https://momaa.org/timeless-luxury-modern-kitchen-design-trends-for-small-spaces-in-2025/" data-wpil-monitor-id="2139">fashion</a>, follows its own trend lines. Of late, it seems to have developed a penchant for diversity and the novel narratives offered by <a href="https://momaa.org/african-contemporary-art/" data-wpil-monitor-id="5225">Contemporary African Art</a>. Even the venerable auction house, Sotheby&#8217;s, has been swept up in this tide, now dedicating an annual <a href="https://momaa.org/reshaping-art-auction-market/" data-wpil-monitor-id="11786">auction to this vibrant art</a> form. This has not only given rise to a competitive <a href="https://momaa.org/art-market-outpaces-gold-and-bitcoin-in-2024-economic-downturn/" data-wpil-monitor-id="567">market but also made affordable art</a> a reality for many an enthusiast.</p>

		</div>
	</div>
<div class="vc_separator wpb_content_element vc_separator_align_center vc_sep_width_100 vc_sep_pos_align_center vc_sep_color_grey wpb_content_element vc_separator-has-text" ><span class="vc_sep_holder vc_sep_holder_l"><span class="vc_sep_line"></span></span><h4>MoMAA | African Modern Affordable Art Gallery</h4><span class="vc_sep_holder vc_sep_holder_r"><span class="vc_sep_line"></span></span>
</div></div></div></div><div class="wpb_column vc_column_container vc_col-sm-3"><div class="vc_column-inner"><div class="wpb_wrapper">
	<div class="wpb_text_column wpb_content_element" >
		<div class="wpb_wrapper">
			<h3>MoMAA&#8217;s Role</h3>
<p>Amidst this <a href="https://momaa.org/10-must-follow-african-artists-on-twitter/" data-wpil-monitor-id="14489">global</a> art bazaar, MoMAA stands as a lighthouse guiding those navigating the exhilarating yet often perplexing world of art. Whether you find yourself musing over a potential acquisition, contemplating commissioning a special piece, or merely exploring the realm of affordable art, <a href="https://momaa.org/" target="_new" rel="noopener">MoMAA</a> is your steadfast companion on this voyage of discovery.</p>
<h2>Our Services</h2>
<h3>Artworks</h3>
<p>The <a href="https://momaa.org/product-category/artworks/" target="_new" rel="noopener">Artworks</a> section at MoMAA is akin to a meticulously curated art exhibition, boasting a vibrant collection of works from Emerging African Artists. Here, every style and technique is celebrated, inviting you to dive headfirst into the world of <a href="https://momaa.org/affordable-art-a-connoisseurs-journey/" data-wpil-monitor-id="8326">affordable art</a>.</p>
<h3>Blog</h3>
<p>The <a href="https://momaa.org/blog/" target="_new" rel="noopener">MoMAA Journal</a> is your personal gazette to the art world. It offers a wealth of knowledge, from profiles of <a href="https://momaa.org/covid-19-artists-art-market/" data-wpil-monitor-id="11787">artists and market</a> trends to erudite discussions on individual pieces. Consider it your personal guide to the <a href="https://momaa.org/africas-art-scene-may-be-booming/" data-wpil-monitor-id="9648">art scene</a>.</p>
<h3>Valuate Artwork</h3>
<p>Pondering over the potential <a href="https://momaa.org/how-the-mona-lisa-evolved-from-artwork-to-cultural-symbol-shaping-modern-music-and-cuisine-through-its-coded-associations-with-mystique-authenticity-and-mass-market-value/" data-wpil-monitor-id="20813">value of an artwork</a> you possess? Our <a href="https://momaa.org/valuate-artwork/" target="_new" rel="noopener">Artwork Valuation</a> service offers a fair and informed appraisal, setting a realistic expectation in the market.</p>
<h3>Sell Art</h3>
<p>If you have a piece of Modern African Art to sell, <a href="https://momaa.org/sell-modern-african-art/" target="_new" rel="noopener">MoMAA</a> is your perfect conduit to reach out to a network of art enthusiasts and collectors, ensuring your work gets the attention it deserves.</p>

		</div>
	</div>
</div></div></div><div class="wpb_column vc_column_container vc_col-sm-3"><div class="vc_column-inner"><div class="wpb_wrapper">
	<div class="wpb_text_column wpb_content_element" >
		<div class="wpb_wrapper">
			<h3>Discover</h3>
<p>Picture, if you will, a grand tour of the African continent, each step taking you deeper into the rich <a href="https://momaa.org/african-artist-spotlight-series-billie-zangewas-intricate-silk-tapestries/" data-wpil-monitor-id="4246">tapestry of its artistic</a> heritage. The <a href="https://momaa.org/discover/" target="_new" rel="noopener">Discover</a> section at MoMAA serves as your personal guide on this extraordinary journey, an exquisite directory of African museums that stands ready to be explored.</p>
<p>Each museum, much like a chapter in a gripping novel, unfolds a unique <a href="https://momaa.org/african-artists-and-mythology-exploring-the-stories-of-the-continent/" data-wpil-monitor-id="9376">story of the continent&#8217;s</a> art, encapsulating the essence of the region it hails from. As you meander through this <a href="https://momaa.org/curator/" data-wpil-monitor-id="18154">curated</a> catalogue, you&#8217;ll stumble upon pieces of affordable art that not only captivate the eye but also stir the soul.</p>
<p>The Discover section is more than a mere directory; it is an open invitation from <a href="https://momaa.org/artists-sell-on-momaa/" data-wpil-monitor-id="11038">MoMAA to embark on a voyage of artistic</a> discovery. To traverse the expanse of the <a href="https://momaa.org/african-artist-spotlight-series-lina-iris-viktors-gilded-canvases/" data-wpil-monitor-id="4243">African artistic</a> landscape from the comfort of your own home, to appreciate the diverse expressions of its artists, and to ultimately unearth that one resonating piece that seems as though it was crafted just for you.</p>
<p>With MoMAA as your steadfast companion, you are not just exploring; you are connecting, learning, and immersing yourself in the vibrant <a href="https://momaa.org/african-artist-spotlight-series-the-ethereal-world-of-joana-choumali/" data-wpil-monitor-id="4245">world of African</a> art. So come, let us traverse this colourful path together, and discover the hidden gems that lie within the heart of <a href="https://momaa.org/africa-day-a-celebration-of-artistic-diversity-and-heritage/" data-wpil-monitor-id="6967">Africa&#8217;s artistic heritage</a>.</p>
<p>MoMAA is more than a gallery &#8211; it is a <a href="https://momaa.org/most-expensive-paintings-2024/" data-wpil-monitor-id="762">lifestyle</a>. A <a href="https://www.nft54.io" target="_blank">space</a> that inspires exploration, cultivates appreciation, and simplifies the acquisition of affordable art. Join us as we celebrate the dynamic and diverse world of <a href="https://momaa.org/african-artist-spotlight-series-the-sculptural-wonders-of-ibrahim-mahama/" data-wpil-monitor-id="3491">contemporary African Art</a>.</p>
<h3>Art Resources</h3>
<p><a href="https://momaa.org/esther-mahlangu-and-the-global-revolution-of-ndebele-art/">Esther Mahlangu and Ndebele Art</a></p>

		</div>
	</div>
</div></div></div><div class="wpb_column vc_column_container vc_col-sm-3"><div class="vc_column-inner"><div class="wpb_wrapper"><h2 style="color: #595959;text-align: center;font-family:Abril Fatface;font-weight:400;font-style:normal" class="vc_custom_heading" >MoMAA | African Modern Affordable Art Gallery</h2>
